<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Asthma</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Long-term inflammatory disease of the airways of the lungs</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Asthma_(disambiguation)" title="Asthma (disambiguation)">Asthma (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p169-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p214_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p214-8">[8]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" class="infobox-label" scope="row">Deaths</th><td class="infobox-data">approx. 461,000 (2019)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancetasthma_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-lancetasthma-9">[9]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Asthma</b> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chronic_(medicine)" title="Chronic (medicine)">long-term</a> <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammatory</a> disease of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronchi" title="Bronchi">airways</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lungs" title="Lungs">lungs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup> It is characterized by variable and recurring symptoms, reversible <a href="/wiki/Airway_obstruction" title="Airway obstruction">airflow obstruction</a>, and easily triggered <a href="/wiki/Bronchospasm" title="Bronchospasm">bronchospasms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p11-12_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p11-12-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA_2011_page20,51_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA_2011_page20,51-11">[11]</a></sup> Symptoms include episodes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wheezing" title="Wheezing">wheezing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coughing" title="Coughing">coughing</a>, chest tightness, and <a href="/wiki/Shortness_of_breath" title="Shortness of breath">shortness of breath</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goldman2020_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Goldman2020-4">[4]</a></sup> These may occur a few times a day or a few times per week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup> Depending on the person, asthma symptoms may become worse at night or with exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Asthma is thought to be caused by a combination of <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_factor" title="Environmental factor">environmental factors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goldman2020_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Goldman2020-4">[4]</a></sup> Environmental factors include exposure to <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allergen" title="Allergen">allergens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup> Other potential triggers include medications such as <a href="/wiki/Aspirin" title="Aspirin">aspirin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beta_blockers" title="Beta blockers">beta blockers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup> Diagnosis is usually based on the pattern of symptoms, response to therapy over time, and <a href="/wiki/Spirometry" title="Spirometry">spirometry</a> lung function testing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lemanske2010_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lemanske2010-6">[6]</a></sup> Asthma is classified according to the frequency of symptoms, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_expiratory_volume_in_one_second" title="Forced expiratory volume in one second">forced expiratory volume in one second</a> (FEV1), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peak_expiratory_flow_rate" title="Peak expiratory flow rate">peak expiratory flow rate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yawn2008_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yawn2008-12">[12]</a></sup> It may also be classified as <a href="/wiki/Atopy" title="Atopy">atopic</a> or non-atopic, where atopy refers to a predisposition toward developing a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Type_1_hypersensitivity" title="Type 1 hypersensitivity">type 1 hypersensitivity</a> reaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobbinsCotran2010_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobbinsCotran2010-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is no known cure for asthma, but can be controlled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup> Symptoms can be prevented by avoiding triggers, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allergens" title="Allergens">allergens</a> and respiratory <a href="/wiki/Irritation" title="Irritation">irritants</a>, and suppressed with the use of inhaled <a href="/wiki/Corticosteroid" title="Corticosteroid">corticosteroids</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p169_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p169-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA_2011_page71_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA_2011_page71-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Long-acting_beta-adrenoceptor_agonist" title="Long-acting beta-adrenoceptor agonist">Long-acting beta agonists</a> (LABA) or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antileukotriene_agent" title="Antileukotriene agent">antileukotriene agents</a> may be used in addition to inhaled corticosteroids if asthma symptoms remain uncontrolled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA_2011_page33_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA_2011_page33-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antileukotriene_agents_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Antileukotriene_agents-17">[17]</a></sup> Treatment of rapidly worsening symptoms is usually with an inhaled short-acting <a href="/wiki/Beta2-adrenergic_agonist" title="Beta2-adrenergic agonist">beta-2 agonist</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Salbutamol" title="Salbutamol">salbutamol</a> and corticosteroids taken by mouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p214_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p214-8">[8]</a></sup> In very severe cases, intravenous corticosteroids, <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_sulfate" title="Magnesium sulfate">magnesium sulfate</a>, and hospitalization may be required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p373_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p373-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019 asthma affected approximately 262 million people and caused approximately 461,000 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancetasthma_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-lancetasthma-9">[9]</a></sup> Most of the deaths occurred in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">developing world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup> Asthma often begins in childhood,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2013_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2013-5">[5]</a></sup> and the rates have increased significantly since the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ana2010_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ana2010-19">[19]</a></sup> Asthma was recognized as early as <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egypt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manniche1999_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manniche1999-20">[20]</a></sup> The word "asthma" is from the Greek <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">ἆσθμα</span></span>, <i>âsthma</i>, which means "panting".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Signs_and_symptoms"><span class="anchor" id="Asthma_attack"></span>Signs and symptoms</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097025294">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:Wheeze2O_noise_reduced.ogg" title="File:Wheeze2O noise reduced.ogg">Wheezing</a></div>
<div><audio controls="" data-durationhint="11" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Wheeze2O_noise_reduced.ogg" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:232px;" width="232"><source data-bandwidth="28989" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (29 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9b/Wheeze2O_noise_reduced.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="67600" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/9b/Wheeze2O_noise_reduced.ogg/Wheeze2O_noise_reduced.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio></div>
<div class="description">The sound of wheezing as heard with a stethoscope.</div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr/><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>Asthma is characterized by recurrent episodes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wheezing" title="Wheezing">wheezing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shortness_of_breath" title="Shortness of breath">shortness of breath</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_tightness" title="Chest tightness">chest tightness</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cough" title="Cough">coughing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011p2_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011p2-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sputum" title="Sputum">Sputum</a> may be produced from the lung by coughing but is often hard to bring up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> During recovery from an asthma attack (exacerbation), it may appear <a href="/wiki/Pus" title="Pus">pus-like</a> due to high levels of white blood cells called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eosinophils" title="Eosinophils">eosinophils</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Symptoms are usually worse at night and in the early morning or in response to exercise or cold air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bts2009p14_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-bts2009p14-25">[25]</a></sup> Some people with asthma rarely experience symptoms, usually in response to triggers, whereas others may react frequently and readily and experience persistent symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011_p8-9_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011_p8-9-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Associated_conditions">Associated conditions</span></h3>
<p>A number of other health conditions occur more frequently in people with asthma, including <a href="/wiki/Gastroesophageal_reflux_disease" title="Gastroesophageal reflux disease">gastroesophageal reflux disease</a> (GERD), <a href="/wiki/Rhinosinusitis" title="Rhinosinusitis">rhinosinusitis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Obstructive_sleep_apnea" title="Obstructive sleep apnea">obstructive sleep apnea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boulet2009_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boulet2009-27">[27]</a></sup> Psychological disorders are also more common,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boulay2011_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boulay2011-28">[28]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety disorders</a> occurring in between 16 and 52% and <a href="/wiki/Mood_disorder" title="Mood disorder">mood disorders</a> in 14–41%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrew2010_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew2010-29">[29]</a></sup> It is not known whether asthma causes psychological problems or psychological problems lead to asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Current asthma, but not former asthma, is associated with increased all-cause mortality, heart disease mortality, and chronic lower respiratory tract disease mortality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Asthma, particularly severe asthma, is strongly associated with development of chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Those with asthma, especially if it is poorly controlled, are at increased risk for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiocontrast" title="Radiocontrast">radiocontrast</a> reactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tooth_decay" title="Tooth decay">Cavities</a> occur more often in people with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> This may be related to the effect of <a href="/wiki/Beta2-adrenergic_agonist" title="Beta2-adrenergic agonist">beta 2 agonists</a> decreasing saliva.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tho2010_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tho2010-37">[37]</a></sup> These medications may also increase the risk of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_erosion" title="Dental erosion">dental erosions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tho2010_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tho2010-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Causes">Causes</span></h2>
<p>Asthma is caused by a combination of complex and incompletely understood environmental and genetic interactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martinez2007_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martinez2007-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> These influence both its severity and its responsiveness to treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> It is believed that the recent increased rates of asthma are due to changing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epigenetic" title="Epigenetic">epigenetics</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heritable" title="Heritable">heritable</a> factors other than those related to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DNA_sequence" title="DNA sequence">DNA sequence</a>) and a changing living environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21575714_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21575714-41">[41]</a></sup> Asthma that starts before the age of 12 years old is more likely due to genetic influence, while onset after age 12 is more likely due to environmental influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental">Environmental</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Asthma-related_microbes" title="Asthma-related microbes">Asthma-related microbes</a></div>

<p>Many environmental factors have been associated with asthma's development and exacerbation, including, allergens, air pollution, and other environmental chemicals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21623970_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21623970-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Smoking_and_pregnancy" title="Smoking and pregnancy">Smoking during pregnancy</a> and after delivery is associated with a greater risk of asthma-like symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011_p6_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011_p6-44">[44]</a></sup> Low <a href="/wiki/Air_quality_index" title="Air quality index">air quality</a> from environmental factors such as <a href="/wiki/Exhaust_gas" title="Exhaust gas">traffic pollution</a> or high <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> levels<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011_p61_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011_p61-45">[45]</a></sup> has been associated with both asthma development and increased asthma severity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gold_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gold-46">[46]</a></sup> Over half of cases in children in the United States occur in areas when air quality is below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EPA" title="EPA">EPA</a> standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Low air quality is more common in <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic_status" title="Socioeconomic status">low-income</a> and minority communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Exposure to indoor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compounds" title="Volatile organic compounds">volatile organic compounds</a> may be a trigger for asthma; <a href="/wiki/Formaldehyde" title="Formaldehyde">formaldehyde</a> exposure, for example, has a positive association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid20064771_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20064771-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phthalate" title="Phthalate">Phthalates</a> in certain types of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PVC" title="PVC">PVC</a> are associated with asthma in both children and adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid20059582_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20059582-51">[51]</a></sup> While exposure to <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a> is linked to the development of asthma, a cause and effect relationship has yet to be established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MamJune2015_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-MamJune2015-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MamSept2015_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-MamSept2015-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of the evidence does not support a causal role between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acetaminophen" title="Acetaminophen">acetaminophen</a> (paracetamol) or antibiotic use and asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> A 2014 systematic review found that the association between acetaminophen use and asthma disappeared when respiratory infections were taken into account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Acetaminophen use by a mother during pregnancy is also associated with an increased risk of the child developing asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Maternal <a href="/wiki/Psychological_stress" title="Psychological stress">psychological stress</a> during pregnancy is a risk factor for the child to develop asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>Asthma is associated with exposure to indoor allergens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21301330_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21301330-59">[59]</a></sup> Common indoor allergens include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dust_mite" title="Dust mite">dust mites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cockroach" title="Cockroach">cockroaches</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_dander" title="Animal dander">animal dander</a> (fragments of fur or feathers), and mold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arshad_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arshad-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Efforts to decrease dust mites have been found to be ineffective on symptoms in sensitized subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gotzsche2008_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gotzsche2008-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Weak evidence suggests that efforts to decrease mold by repairing buildings may help improve asthma symptoms in adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Certain viral respiratory infections, such as <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_syncytial_virus" title="Respiratory syncytial virus">respiratory syncytial virus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhinovirus" title="Rhinovirus">rhinovirus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup> may increase the risk of developing asthma when acquired as young children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p11_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p11-65">[65]</a></sup> Certain other infections, however, may decrease the risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hygiene_hypothesis">Hygiene hypothesis</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hygiene_hypothesis" title="Hygiene hypothesis">hygiene hypothesis</a> attempts to explain the increased rates of asthma worldwide as a direct and unintended result of reduced exposure, during childhood, to non-pathogenic bacteria and viruses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> It has been proposed that the reduced exposure to bacteria and viruses is due, in part, to increased cleanliness and decreased family size in modern societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brook2013_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brook2013-68">[68]</a></sup> Exposure to bacterial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endotoxin" title="Endotoxin">endotoxin</a> in early childhood may prevent the development of asthma, but exposure at an older age may provoke bronchoconstriction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Evidence supporting the hygiene hypothesis includes lower rates of asthma on farms and in households with pets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brook2013_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brook2013-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>Use of <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotics</a> in early life has been linked to the development of asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Also, delivery via <a href="/wiki/Caesarean_section" title="Caesarean section">caesarean section</a> is associated with an increased risk (estimated at 20–80%) of asthma – this increased risk is attributed to the lack of healthy bacterial colonization that the newborn would have acquired from passage through the birth canal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21645799_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21645799-72">[72]</a></sup> There is a link between asthma and the degree of affluence which may be related to the hygiene hypothesis as less affluent individuals often have more exposure to bacteria and viruses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid14763924_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid14763924-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic">Genetic</span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left:15px; text-align:center">
<caption>CD14-endotoxin interaction based on CD14 SNP C-159T<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martinez_CD14_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martinez_CD14-74">[74]</a></sup>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Endotoxin levels</th>
<th>CC genotype</th>
<th>TT genotype
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>High exposure
</th>
<td>Low risk</td>
<td>High risk
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Low exposure
</th>
<td>High risk</td>
<td>Low risk
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Family history is a risk factor for asthma, with many different genes being implicated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El2010_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-El2010-75">[75]</a></sup> If one identical twin is affected, the probability of the other having the disease is approximately 25%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El2010_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-El2010-75">[75]</a></sup> By the end of 2005, 25 genes had been associated with asthma in six or more separate populations, including <a href="/wiki/Glutathione_S-transferase_Mu_1" title="Glutathione S-transferase Mu 1">GSTM1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interleukin_10" title="Interleukin 10">IL10</a>, <a href="/wiki/CTLA-4" title="CTLA-4">CTLA-4</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SPINK5" title="SPINK5">SPINK5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leukotriene_C4_synthase" title="Leukotriene C4 synthase">LTC4S</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interleukin-4_receptor" title="Interleukin-4 receptor">IL4R</a> and <a href="/wiki/ADAM33" title="ADAM33">ADAM33</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffjan_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffjan-76">[76]</a></sup> Many of these genes are related to the immune system or modulating inflammation. Even among this list of genes supported by highly replicated studies, results have not been consistent among all populations tested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffjan_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffjan-76">[76]</a></sup> In 2006 over 100 <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> were associated with asthma in one <a href="/wiki/Genetic_association" title="Genetic association">genetic association</a> study alone;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffjan_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffjan-76">[76]</a></sup> more continue to be found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid20298365_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20298365-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some genetic variants may only cause asthma when they are combined with specific environmental exposures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martinez2007_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Martinez2007-38">[38]</a></sup> An example is a specific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_nucleotide_polymorphism" title="Single nucleotide polymorphism">single nucleotide polymorphism</a> in the <a href="/wiki/CD14" title="CD14">CD14</a> region and exposure to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endotoxin" title="Endotoxin">endotoxin</a> (a bacterial product). Endotoxin exposure can come from several environmental sources including tobacco smoke, dogs, and farms. Risk for asthma, then, is determined by both a person's genetics and the level of endotoxin exposure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martinez_CD14_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Martinez_CD14-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_conditions">Medical conditions</span></h3>
<p>A triad of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atopic_eczema" title="Atopic eczema">atopic eczema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allergic_rhinitis" title="Allergic rhinitis">allergic rhinitis</a> and asthma is called atopy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolognia_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bolognia-78">[78]</a></sup> The strongest risk factor for developing asthma is a history of <a href="/wiki/Atopy" title="Atopy">atopic disease</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p11_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p11-65">[65]</a></sup> with asthma occurring at a much greater rate in those who have either <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eczema" title="Eczema">eczema</a> or <a href="/wiki/Rhinitis" title="Rhinitis">hay fever</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011_p4_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011_p4-79">[79]</a></sup> Asthma has been associated with <a href="/wiki/Eosinophilic_granulomatosis_with_polyangiitis" title="Eosinophilic granulomatosis with polyangiitis">eosinophilic granulomatosis with polyangiitis</a> (formerly known as Churg–Strauss syndrome), an autoimmune disease and <a href="/wiki/Vasculitis" title="Vasculitis">vasculitis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChapelHill_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChapelHill-80">[80]</a></sup> Individuals with certain types of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urticaria" title="Urticaria">urticaria</a> may also experience symptoms of asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolognia_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bolognia-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a correlation between <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a> and the risk of asthma with both having increased in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-holguin_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-holguin-82">[82]</a></sup> Several factors may be at play including decreased respiratory function due to a buildup of fat and the fact that adipose tissue leads to a pro-inflammatory state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woods_2009_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Woods_2009-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Beta_blocker" title="Beta blocker">Beta blocker</a> medications such as <a href="/wiki/Propranolol" title="Propranolol">propranolol</a> can trigger asthma in those who are susceptible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17998992_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17998992-84">[84]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardioselective_beta-blockers" title="Cardioselective beta-blockers">Cardioselective beta-blockers</a>, however, appear safe in those with mild or moderate disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Other medications that can cause problems in asthmatics are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angiotensin-converting_enzyme_inhibitors" title="Angiotensin-converting enzyme inhibitors">angiotensin-converting enzyme inhibitors</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acetylsalicylic_acid" title="Acetylsalicylic acid">aspirin</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NSAIDs" title="NSAIDs">NSAIDs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid15579370_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid15579370-87">[87]</a></sup> Use of acid suppressing medication (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proton_pump_inhibitors" title="Proton pump inhibitors">proton pump inhibitors</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H2_blockers" title="H2 blockers">H2 blockers</a>) during pregnancy is associated with an increased risk of asthma in the child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exacerbation">Exacerbation</span></h3>
<p>Some individuals will have stable asthma for weeks or months and then suddenly develop an episode of acute asthma. Different individuals react to various factors in different ways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baxi2010_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baxi2010-89">[89]</a></sup> Most individuals can develop severe exacerbation from a number of triggering agents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baxi2010_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-Baxi2010-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Home factors that can lead to exacerbation of asthma include <a href="/wiki/Dust" title="Dust">dust</a>, animal <a href="/wiki/Dander" title="Dander">dander</a> (especially cat and dog hair), cockroach <a href="/wiki/Allergen" title="Allergen">allergens</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mold_(fungus)" title="Mold (fungus)">mold</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baxi2010_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-Baxi2010-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Perfume" title="Perfume">Perfumes</a> are a common cause of acute attacks in women and children. Both <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viral</a> and bacterial <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infections</a> of the upper respiratory tract can worsen the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baxi2010_89-3"><a href="#cite_note-Baxi2010-89">[89]</a></sup> Psychological <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stress_(biological)" title="Stress (biological)">stress</a> may worsen symptoms – it is thought that stress alters the immune system and thus increases the airway inflammatory response to allergens and irritants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gold_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gold-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chen2007_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chen2007-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>Asthma exacerbations in school‐aged children peak in autumn, shortly after children return to school. This might reflect a combination of factors, including poor treatment adherence, increased allergen and viral exposure, and altered immune tolerance. There is limited evidence to guide possible approaches to reducing autumn exacerbations, but while costly, seasonal <a href="/wiki/Omalizumab" title="Omalizumab">omalizumab</a> treatment from four to six weeks before school return may reduce autumn asthma exacerbations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PikeAkhbari2018_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-PikeAkhbari2018-92">[92]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pathophysiology">Pathophysiology</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pathophysiology_of_asthma" title="Pathophysiology of asthma">Pathophysiology of asthma</a></div>
<p>Asthma is the result of chronic <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammation</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conducting_zone" title="Conducting zone">conducting zone</a> of the airways (most especially the <a href="/wiki/Bronchus" title="Bronchus">bronchi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronchiole" title="Bronchiole">bronchioles</a>), which subsequently results in increased contractability of the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Smooth_muscle" title="Smooth muscle">smooth muscles</a>. This among other factors leads to bouts of narrowing of the airway and the classic symptoms of wheezing. The narrowing is typically reversible with or without treatment. Occasionally the airways themselves change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011p2_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011p2-22">[22]</a></sup> Typical changes in the airways include an increase in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eosinophils" title="Eosinophils">eosinophils</a> and thickening of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lamina_reticularis" title="Lamina reticularis">lamina reticularis</a>. Chronically the airways' smooth muscle may increase in size along with an increase in the numbers of mucous glands. Other cell types involved include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T_lymphocytes" title="T lymphocytes">T lymphocytes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macrophages" title="Macrophages">macrophages</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrophils" title="Neutrophils">neutrophils</a>. There may also be involvement of other components of the <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a>, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cytokines" title="Cytokines">cytokines</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemokines" title="Chemokines">chemokines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Histamine" title="Histamine">histamine</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leukotrienes" title="Leukotrienes">leukotrienes</a> among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis">Diagnosis</span></h2>
<p>While asthma is a well-recognized condition, there is not one universal agreed upon definition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup> It is defined by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Initiative_for_Asthma" title="Global Initiative for Asthma">Global Initiative for Asthma</a> as "a chronic inflammatory disorder of the airways in which many cells and cellular elements play a role. The chronic inflammation is associated with airway hyper-responsiveness that leads to recurrent episodes of wheezing, breathlessness, chest tightness and coughing particularly at night or in the early morning. These episodes are usually associated with widespread but variable airflow obstruction within the lung that is often reversible either spontaneously or with treatment".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011p2_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011p2-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is currently no precise test for the diagnosis, which is typically based on the pattern of symptoms and response to therapy over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lemanske2010_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lemanske2010-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-5"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup> Asthma may be suspected if there is a history of recurrent wheezing, coughing or difficulty breathing and these symptoms occur or worsen due to exercise, viral infections, allergens or air pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAEPP42_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAEPP42-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Spirometry" title="Spirometry">Spirometry</a> is then used to confirm the diagnosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAEPP42_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-NAEPP42-93">[93]</a></sup> In children under the age of six the diagnosis is more difficult as they are too young for spirometry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA2011p20_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA2011p20-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spirometry">Spirometry</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Spirometry" title="Spirometry">Spirometry</a> is recommended to aid in diagnosis and management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAAAIfive_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-AAAAIfive-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHasthmaguide_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIHasthmaguide-96">[96]</a></sup> It is the single best test for asthma. If the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FEV1" title="FEV1">FEV1</a> measured by this technique improves more than 12% and increases by at least 200 milliliters following administration of a <a href="/wiki/Bronchodilator" title="Bronchodilator">bronchodilator</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Salbutamol" title="Salbutamol">salbutamol</a>, this is supportive of the diagnosis. It however may be normal in those with a history of mild asthma, not currently acting up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-6"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/Caffeine" title="Caffeine">caffeine</a> is a bronchodilator in people with asthma, the use of caffeine before a lung function test may interfere with the results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid20091514_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20091514-97">[97]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single-breath_diffusing_capacity" title="Single-breath diffusing capacity">Single-breath diffusing capacity</a> can help differentiate asthma from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COPD" title="COPD">COPD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-7"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup> It is reasonable to perform spirometry every one or two years to follow how well a person's asthma is controlled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p58_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p58-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methacholine_challenge_test" title="Methacholine challenge test">methacholine challenge</a> involves the inhalation of increasing concentrations of a substance that causes airway narrowing in those predisposed. If negative it means that a person does not have asthma; if positive, however, it is not specific for the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-8"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other supportive evidence includes: a ≥20% difference in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peak_expiratory_flow_rate" title="Peak expiratory flow rate">peak expiratory flow rate</a> on at least three days in a week for at least two weeks, a ≥20% improvement of peak flow following treatment with either salbutamol, inhaled corticosteroids or prednisone, or a ≥20% decrease in peak flow following exposure to a trigger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Testing peak expiratory flow is more variable than spirometry, however, and thus not recommended for routine diagnosis. It may be useful for daily self-monitoring in those with moderate to severe disease and for checking the effectiveness of new medications. It may also be helpful in guiding treatment in those with acute exacerbations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAEPP2007p59_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAEPP2007p59-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="clear:right; float:right; margin-left:1em; text-align:center">

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Asthma is clinically classified according to the frequency of symptoms, forced expiratory volume in one second (<a href="/wiki/Spirometry" title="Spirometry">FEV<sub>1</sub></a>), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peak_expiratory_flow_rate" title="Peak expiratory flow rate">peak expiratory flow rate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yawn2008_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Yawn2008-12">[12]</a></sup> Asthma may also be classified as atopic (extrinsic) or non-atopic (intrinsic), based on whether symptoms are precipitated by allergens (atopic) or not (non-atopic).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobbinsCotran2010_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-RobbinsCotran2010-13">[13]</a></sup> While asthma is classified based on severity, at the moment there is no clear method for classifying different subgroups of asthma beyond this system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moore2010_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moore2010-101">[101]</a></sup> Finding ways to identify subgroups that respond well to different types of treatments is a current critical goal of asthma research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moore2010_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Moore2010-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although asthma is a chronic <a href="/wiki/Obstructive_lung_disease" title="Obstructive lung disease">obstructive</a> condition, it is not considered as a part of <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">chronic obstructive pulmonary disease</a>, as this term refers specifically to combinations of disease that are irreversible such as <a href="/wiki/Bronchiectasis" title="Bronchiectasis">bronchiectasis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pneumatosis#Lungs" title="Pneumatosis">emphysema</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Self,_Timothy_2009_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Self,_Timothy_2009-102">[102]</a></sup> Unlike these diseases, the airway obstruction in asthma is usually reversible; however, if left untreated, the chronic inflammation from asthma can lead the lungs to become irreversibly obstructed due to airway remodeling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delacourt2004_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Delacourt2004-103">[103]</a></sup> In contrast to emphysema, asthma affects the bronchi, not the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_alveolus" title="Pulmonary alveolus">alveoli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schiffman2009_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schiffman2009-104">[104]</a></sup> The combination of asthma with a component of irreversible airways obstruction has been termed the asthma-chronic obstructive disease (COPD) overlap syndrome (ACOS). Compared to other people with "pure" asthma or COPD, people with ACOS exhibit increased morbidity, mortality and possibly more comorbidities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Asthma_exacerbation">Asthma exacerbation</span></h4>
<table class="wikitable" style="clear:right; float:right; margin-left:15px; text-align:center">
