</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>An acute asthma exacerbation is commonly referred to as an <i>asthma attack</i>. The classic symptoms are <a href="/wiki/Shortness_of_breath" title="Shortness of breath">shortness of breath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheeze" title="Wheeze">wheezing</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_tightness" title="Chest tightness">chest tightness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M38_21-9"><a href="#cite_note-M38-21">[21]</a></sup> The wheezing is most often when breathing out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> While these are the primary symptoms of asthma,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnes2008_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barnes2008-108">[108]</a></sup> some people present primarily with <a href="/wiki/Cough" title="Cough">coughing</a>, and in severe cases, air motion may be significantly impaired such that no wheezing is heard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BTS58_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-BTS58-106">[106]</a></sup> In children, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pediatric_chest_pain" title="Pediatric chest pain">chest pain</a> is often present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mac2011_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mac2011-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>Signs occurring during an asthma attack include the use of accessory <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscles</a> of respiration (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sternocleidomastoid" title="Sternocleidomastoid">sternocleidomastoid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scalene_muscles" title="Scalene muscles">scalene muscles</a> of the neck), there may be a <a href="/wiki/Pulsus_paradoxus" title="Pulsus paradoxus">paradoxical pulse</a> (a pulse that is weaker during inhalation and stronger during exhalation), and over-inflation of the chest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maitre1995_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maitre1995-110">[110]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Cyanosis" title="Cyanosis">blue color</a> of the skin and nails may occur from lack of oxygen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Werner2001_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Werner2001-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a mild exacerbation the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peak_expiratory_flow_rate" title="Peak expiratory flow rate">peak expiratory flow rate</a> (PEFR) is ≥200 L/min, or ≥50% of the predicted best.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shiber2006_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shiber2006-112">[112]</a></sup> Moderate is defined as between 80 and 200 L/min, or 25% and 50% of the predicted best, while severe is defined as ≤ 80 L/min, or ≤25% of the predicted best.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shiber2006_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shiber2006-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Acute_severe_asthma" title="Acute severe asthma">Acute severe asthma</a>, previously known as status asthmaticus, is an acute exacerbation of asthma that does not respond to standard treatments of bronchodilators and corticosteroids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah2012_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shah2012-113">[113]</a></sup> Half of cases are due to infections with others caused by allergen, air pollution, or insufficient or inappropriate medication use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah2012_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shah2012-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Brittle_asthma" title="Brittle asthma">Brittle asthma</a> is a kind of asthma distinguishable by recurrent, severe attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BTS58_106-2"><a href="#cite_note-BTS58-106">[106]</a></sup> Type 1 brittle asthma is a disease with wide peak flow variability, despite intense medication. Type 2 brittle asthma is background well-controlled asthma with sudden severe exacerbations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BTS58_106-3"><a href="#cite_note-BTS58-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Exercise-induced">Exercise-induced</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exercise-induced_bronchoconstriction" title="Exercise-induced bronchoconstriction">Exercise-induced bronchoconstriction</a></div>
<p>Exercise can trigger <a href="/wiki/Bronchoconstriction" title="Bronchoconstriction">bronchoconstriction</a> both in people with or without asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIB2012_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-EIB2012-114">[114]</a></sup> It occurs in most people with asthma and up to 20% of people without asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIB2012_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-EIB2012-114">[114]</a></sup> Exercise-induced bronchoconstriction is common in professional athletes. The highest rates are among cyclists (up to 45%), swimmers, and cross-country skiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wuestenfeld_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wuestenfeld-115">[115]</a></sup> While it may occur with any weather conditions, it is more common when it is dry and cold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA_2011_page17_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA_2011_page17-116">[116]</a></sup> Inhaled beta2-agonists do not appear to improve athletic performance among those without asthma,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18394123_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18394123-117">[117]</a></sup> however, oral doses may improve endurance and strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17241101_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17241101-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21142283_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21142283-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupational">Occupational</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Occupational_asthma" title="Occupational asthma">Occupational asthma</a></div>
<p>Asthma as a result of (or worsened by) workplace exposures is a commonly reported <a href="/wiki/Occupational_disease" title="Occupational disease">occupational disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baur2012_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baur2012-120">[120]</a></sup> Many cases, however, are not reported or recognized as such.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> It is estimated that 5–25% of asthma cases in adults are work-related. A few hundred different agents have been implicated, with the most common being: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isocyanates" title="Isocyanates">isocyanates</a>, grain and wood dust, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colophony" title="Colophony">colophony</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soldering_flux" title="Soldering flux">soldering flux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latex" title="Latex">latex</a>, animals, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aldehydes" title="Aldehydes">aldehydes</a>. The employment associated with the highest risk of problems include: those who <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spray_paint" title="Spray paint">spray paint</a>, bakers and those who process food, nurses, chemical workers, those who work with animals, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welders" title="Welders">welders</a>, hairdressers and timber workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baur2012_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Baur2012-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aspirin-induced_asthma">Aspirin-induced asthma</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspirin-exacerbated_respiratory_disease" title="Aspirin-exacerbated respiratory disease">Aspirin-exacerbated respiratory disease</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspirin-exacerbated_respiratory_disease" title="Aspirin-exacerbated respiratory disease">Aspirin-exacerbated respiratory disease</a> (AERD), also known as <a href="/wiki/Aspirin" title="Aspirin">aspirin</a>-induced asthma, affects up to 9% of asthmatics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> AERD consists of asthma, nasal polyps, sinus disease, and respiratory reactions to aspirin and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NSAID_medications" title="NSAID medications">NSAID medications</a> (such as ibuprofen and naproxen).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> People often also develop loss of smell and most experience respiratory reactions to alcohol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ken2018_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ken2018-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Alcohol-induced_asthma">Alcohol-induced asthma</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alcohol-induced_respiratory_reactions" title="Alcohol-induced respiratory reactions">Alcohol-induced respiratory reactions</a></div>
<p>Alcohol may worsen asthmatic symptoms in up to a third of people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams2013_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adams2013-126">[126]</a></sup> This may be even more common in some ethnic groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese</a> and those with aspirin-induced asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams2013_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-Adams2013-126">[126]</a></sup> Other studies have found improvement in asthmatic symptoms from alcohol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams2013_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-Adams2013-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-atopic_asthma">Non-atopic asthma</span></h4>
<p>Non-atopic asthma, also known as intrinsic or non-allergic, makes up between 10 and 33% of cases. There is negative skin test to common inhalant allergens. Often it starts later in life, and women are more commonly affected than men. Usual treatments may not work as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peter2014_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peter2014-127">[127]</a></sup> The concept that "non-atopic" is synonymous with "non-allergic" is called into question by epidemiological data that the prevalence of asthma is closely related to the serum IgE level standardized for age and sex (P&lt;0.0001), indicating that asthma is almost always associated with some sort of IgE-related reaction and therefore has an allergic basis, although not all the allergic stimuli that cause asthma appear to have been included in the battery of aeroallergens studied (the "missing antigen(s)" hypothesis).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> For example, an updated systematic review and meta-analysis of population-attributable risk (PAR) of <i>Chlamydia pneumoniae</i> biomarkers in chronic asthma found that the PAR for <i>C. pneumoniae</i>-specific IgE was 47%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Infectious_asthma">Infectious asthma</span></h4>
<p>When queried, asthma patients may report that their first asthma symptoms began after an acute lower respiratory tract illness. This type of history has been labelled the "infectious asthma" (IA) syndrome,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Infectious_asthma:_a_reemerging_cli_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Infectious_asthma:_a_reemerging_cli-130">[130]</a></sup> or as "asthma associated with infection" (AAWI)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> to distinguish infection-associated asthma initiation from the well known association of respiratory infections with asthma exacerbations. Reported prevalences of IA for adults range from around 40% in a primary care practice<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Infectious_asthma:_a_reemerging_cli_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-Infectious_asthma:_a_reemerging_cli-130">[130]</a></sup> to 70% in a specialty practice treating mainly severe asthma patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The true population prevalence  of IA in adult-onset asthma is unknown because clinicians are not trained to elicit this type of history routinely, and recollection in child-onset asthma is challenging.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Differential_diagnosis">Differential diagnosis</span></h3>
<p>Many other conditions can cause symptoms similar to those of asthma. In children, symptoms may be due to other upper airway diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Allergic_rhinitis" title="Allergic rhinitis">allergic rhinitis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sinusitis" title="Sinusitis">sinusitis</a>, as well as other causes of airway obstruction including <a href="/wiki/Foreign_body_aspiration" title="Foreign body aspiration">foreign body aspiration</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tracheal_stenosis" title="Tracheal stenosis">tracheal stenosis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laryngotracheomalacia" title="Laryngotracheomalacia">laryngotracheomalacia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vascular_ring" title="Vascular ring">vascular rings</a>, enlarged <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lymph_nodes" title="Lymph nodes">lymph nodes</a> or neck masses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAEPP46_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAEPP46-133">[133]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bronchiolitis" title="Bronchiolitis">Bronchiolitis</a> and other viral infections may also produce wheezing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In adults, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COPD" title="COPD">COPD</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congestive_heart_failure" title="Congestive heart failure">congestive heart failure</a>, airway masses, as well as drug-induced coughing due to <a href="/wiki/ACE_inhibitor" title="ACE inhibitor">ACE inhibitors</a> may cause similar symptoms. In both populations <a href="/wiki/Vocal_cord_dysfunction" title="Vocal cord dysfunction">vocal cord dysfunction</a> may present similarly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAEPP46_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-NAEPP46-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease</a> can coexist with asthma and can occur as a complication of chronic asthma. After the age of 65, most people with obstructive airway disease will have asthma and COPD. In this setting, COPD can be differentiated by increased airway neutrophils, abnormally increased wall thickness, and increased smooth muscle in the bronchi. However, this level of investigation is not performed due to COPD and asthma sharing similar principles of management: corticosteroids, long-acting beta-agonists, and smoking cessation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gibson_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson-135">[135]</a></sup> It closely resembles asthma in symptoms, is correlated with more exposure to cigarette smoke, an older age, less symptom reversibility after bronchodilator administration, and decreased likelihood of family history of atopy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16880365_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16880365-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Applied_Therapeutics_2009_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Applied_Therapeutics_2009-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevention">Prevention</span></h2>
<p>The evidence for the effectiveness of measures to prevent the development of asthma is weak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p184_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p184-138">[138]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> recommends decreasing risk factors such as tobacco smoke, air pollution, chemical irritants including <a href="/wiki/Perfume" title="Perfume">perfume</a>, and the number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_respiratory_infections" title="Lower respiratory infections">lower respiratory infections</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2017Fact_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2017Fact-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Other efforts that show promise include: limiting smoke exposure <a href="/wiki/Uterus" title="Uterus">in utero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breastfeeding" title="Breastfeeding">breastfeeding</a>, and increased exposure to daycare or large families, but none are well supported enough to be recommended for this indication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p184_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p184-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early pet exposure may be useful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22235226_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22235226-141">[141]</a></sup> Results from exposure to pets at other times are inconclusive<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid20053584_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20053584-142">[142]</a></sup> and it is only recommended that pets be removed from the home if a person has allergic symptoms to said pet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Au2005_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Au2005-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>Dietary restrictions during pregnancy or when breast feeding have not been found to be effective at preventing asthma in children and are not recommended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Au2005_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-Au2005-143">[143]</a></sup> Omega-3 consumption, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_diet" title="Mediterranean diet">mediterranean diet</a> and anti-oxidants have been suggested by some studies that might help preventing crisis but the evidence is still inconclusive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Reducing or eliminating compounds known to sensitive people from the work place may be effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baur2012_120-2"><a href="#cite_note-Baur2012-120">[120]</a></sup> It is not clear if annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Influenza_vaccines" title="Influenza vaccines">influenza vaccinations</a> affects the risk of exacerbations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Immunization, however, is recommended by the World Health Organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Smoking bans are effective in decreasing exacerbations of asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Effect_of_smoke-free_legislation_on_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Effect_of_smoke-free_legislation_on-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span></h2>
<p>While there is no cure for asthma, symptoms can typically be improved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The most effective treatment for asthma is identifying triggers, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_effects_of_tobacco_smoking" title="Health effects of tobacco smoking">cigarette smoke</a>, pets, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspirin-induced_asthma" title="Aspirin-induced asthma">aspirin</a>, and eliminating exposure to them. If trigger avoidance is insufficient, the use of medication is recommended. Pharmaceutical drugs are selected based on, among other things, the severity of illness and the frequency of symptoms. Specific medications for asthma are broadly classified into fast-acting and long-acting categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p213_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p213-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGMA08_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-BGMA08-150">[150]</a></sup> The medications listed below have demonstrated efficacy in improving asthma symptoms, however "real world" use-effectiveness is limited as around half of people with asthma worldwide remain sub-optimally controlled, even when treated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> People with asthma may remain sub-optimally controlled either because optimum doses of asthma medications do not work (called "refractory" asthma) or because individuals are either unable (e.g. inability to afford treatment, poor inhaler technique) or unwilling (e.g., wish to avoid side effects of corticosteroids) to take optimum doses of prescribed asthma medications (called "difficult to treat" asthma). In practice, it is not possible to distinguish "refractory" from "difficult to treat" categories for patients who have never taken optimum doses of asthma medications. A related issue is that the asthma efficacy trials upon which the pharmacological treatment guidelines are based have systematically excluded the majority of people with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> For example, asthma efficacy treatment trials always exclude otherwise eligible people who smoke, and smoking blunts the efficacy of inhaled corticosteroids, the mainstay of asthma control management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronchodilators" title="Bronchodilators">Bronchodilators</a> are recommended for short-term relief of symptoms. In those with occasional attacks, no other medication is needed. If mild persistent disease is present (more than two attacks a week), low-dose inhaled corticosteroids or alternatively, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leukotriene_antagonist" title="Leukotriene antagonist">leukotriene antagonist</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Mast_cell_stabilizer" title="Mast cell stabilizer">mast cell stabilizer</a> by mouth is recommended. For those who have daily attacks, a higher dose of inhaled corticosteroids is used. In a moderate or severe exacerbation, corticosteroids by mouth are added to these treatments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p214_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p214-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>People with asthma have higher rates of <a href="/wiki/Anxiety" title="Anxiety">anxiety</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychological_stress" title="Psychological stress">psychological stress</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">depression</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kew2016_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kew2016-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> This is associated with poorer asthma control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kew2016_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kew2016-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_behavioral_therapy" title="Cognitive behavioral therapy">Cognitive behavioral therapy</a> may improve quality of life, asthma control, and anxiety levels in people with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kew2016_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kew2016-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>Improving people's knowledge about asthma and using a written action plan has been identified as an important component of managing asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Providing educational sessions that include information specific to a person's culture is likely effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCallumMorris2017_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCallumMorris2017-162">[162]</a></sup> More research is necessary to determine if increasing preparedness and knowledge of asthma among school staff and families using home-based and school interventions results in long term improvements in safety for children with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> School-based asthma self-management interventions, which attempt to improve knowledge of asthma, its triggers and the importance of regular practitioner review, may reduce hospital admissions and emergency department visits. These interventions may also reduce the number of days children experience asthma symptoms and may lead to small improvements in asthma-related quality of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> More research is necessary to determine if <a href="/wiki/Shared_decision-making_in_medicine" title="Shared decision-making in medicine">shared-decision-making</a> is helpful for managing adults with asthma<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> or if a personalized asthma action plan is effective and necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Some people with asthma use <a href="/wiki/Pulse_oximetry" title="Pulse oximetry">pulse oximeters</a> to monitor their own blood oxygen levels during an asthma attack. However, there is no evidence regarding the use in these instances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lifestyle_modification">Lifestyle modification</span></h3>
<p>Avoidance of triggers is a key component of improving control and preventing attacks. The most common triggers include <a href="/wiki/Allergen" title="Allergen">allergens</a>, smoke (from tobacco or other sources), air pollution, <a href="/wiki/Beta_blocker#Nonselective_agents" title="Beta blocker">non selective beta-blockers</a>, and sulfite-containing foods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAEPP2007p69_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAEPP2007p69-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thomson_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-thomson-171">[171]</a></sup> Cigarette smoking and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second-hand_smoke" title="Second-hand smoke">second-hand smoke</a> (passive smoke) may reduce the effectiveness of medications such as corticosteroids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stap2011_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stap2011-172">[172]</a></sup> Laws that limit smoking decrease the number of people hospitalized for asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Effect_of_smoke-free_legislation_on_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Effect_of_smoke-free_legislation_on-147">[147]</a></sup> Dust mite control measures, including air filtration, chemicals to kill mites, vacuuming, mattress covers and others methods had no effect on asthma symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gotzsche2008_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gotzsche2008-62">[62]</a></sup> There is insufficient evidence to suggest that dehumidifiers are helpful for controlling asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>Overall, exercise is beneficial in people with stable asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Yoga could provide small improvements in quality of life and symptoms in people with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> More research is necessary to determine how effective weight loss is on improving quality of life, the usage of health care services, and adverse effects for people of all ages with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medications"><span class="anchor" id="Anti-asthmatic"></span>Medications</span></h3>
<p>Medications used to treat asthma are divided into two general classes: quick-relief medications used to treat acute symptoms; and long-term control medications used to prevent further exacerbation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p213_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p213-149">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">Antibiotics</a> are generally not needed for sudden worsening of symptoms or for treating asthma at any time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medications_of_asthma_exacerbations">Medications of asthma exacerbations</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Salbutamol2.JPG"><img alt="A round canister above a blue plastic holder" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3321" data-file-width="2318" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Salbutamol2.JPG/220px-Salbutamol2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Salbutamol2.JPG/330px-Salbutamol2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Salbutamol2.JPG/440px-Salbutamol2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Salbutamol2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Salbutamol" title="Salbutamol">Salbutamol</a> metered dose inhaler commonly used to treat asthma attacks.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>Short-acting <a href="/wiki/Beta2-adrenergic_agonist" title="Beta2-adrenergic agonist">beta<sub>2</sub>-adrenoceptor agonists</a> (SABA), such as <a href="/wiki/Salbutamol" title="Salbutamol">salbutamol</a> (<i>albuterol</i> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Adopted_Name" title="United States Adopted Name">USAN</a>) are the first line treatment for asthma symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p214_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p214-8">[8]</a></sup> They are recommended before exercise in those with exercise induced symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anticholinergic" title="Anticholinergic">Anticholinergic</a> medications, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ipratropium" title="Ipratropium">ipratropium</a>, provide additional benefit when used in combination with SABA in those with moderate or severe symptoms and may prevent hospitalizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p214_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p214-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-182">[182]</a></sup> Anticholinergic bronchodilators can also be used if a person cannot tolerate a SABA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Self,_Timothy_2009_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Self,_Timothy_2009-102">[102]</a></sup> If a child requires admission to hospital additional ipratropium does not appear to help over a SABA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> For children over 2 years old with acute asthma symptoms, inhaled anticholinergic medications taken alone is safe but is not as effective as inhaled SABA or SABA combined with inhaled anticholinergic medication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-181">[181]</a></sup> Adults who receive combined inhaled medications that includes short-acting anticholinergics and SABA may be at risk for increased adverse effects such as experiencing a tremor, agitation, and heart beat <a href="/wiki/Palpitations" title="Palpitations">palpitations</a> compared to people who are treated with SABA by itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_182-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-182">[182]</a></sup></li>
<li>Older, less selective <a href="/wiki/Adrenergic_receptor" title="Adrenergic receptor">adrenergic agonists</a>, such as inhaled <a href="/wiki/Epinephrine_(medication)" title="Epinephrine (medication)">epinephrine</a>, have similar efficacy to SABAs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodrigo_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rodrigo-185">[185]</a></sup> They are however not recommended due to concerns regarding excessive cardiac stimulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p351_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p351-186">[186]</a></sup></li>
<li>Corticosteroids can also help with the acute phase of an exacerbation because of their antiinflamatory properties. The benefit of systemic and oral corticosteroids is well established. Inhaled or nebulized corticosteroids can also be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup> For adults and children who are in the hospital due to acute asthma, systemic (IV) corticosteroids improve symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> A short course of corticosteroids after an acute asthma exacerbation may help prevent relapses and reduce hospitalizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></li>
<li>Other remedies, less established, are intravenous or nebulized magnesium sulfate and helium mixed with oxygen. Aminophylline could be used with caution as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-2"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li>Mechanical ventilation is the last resort in case of severe hypoxemia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-3"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li>Intravenous administration of the drug <a href="/wiki/Aminophylline" title="Aminophylline">aminophylline</a> does not provide an improvement in bronchodilation when compared to standard inhaled beta-2 agonist treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nai2012_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nai2012-190">[190]</a></sup> Aminophylline treatment is associated with more adverse effects compared to inhaled beta-2 agonist treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nai2012_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nai2012-190">[190]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span id="Long.E2.80.93term_control"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Long–term_control">Long–term control</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fluticasone.JPG"><img alt="A round canister above an orange plastic holder" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3734" data-file-width="2656" decoding="async" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fluticasone.JPG/220px-Fluticasone.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fluticasone.JPG/330px-Fluticasone.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fluticasone.JPG/440px-Fluticasone.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fluticasone.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fluticasone_propionate" title="Fluticasone propionate">Fluticasone propionate</a> metered dose inhaler commonly used for long-term control.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>Corticosteroids are generally considered the most effective treatment available for long-term control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p213_149-2"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p213-149">[149]</a></sup> Inhaled forms are usually used except in the case of severe persistent disease, in which oral corticosteroids may be needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p213_149-3"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p213-149">[149]</a></sup> Dosage depends on the severity of symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p218_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p218-191">[191]</a></sup> High dosage and long term use might lead to the appearance of common adverse effects which are  growth delay, adrenal suppression, and osteoporosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-4"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup> Continuous (daily) use of an inhaled corticosteroid, rather than its intermitted use, seems to provide better results in controlling asthma exacerbations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-5"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup> Commonly used corticosteroids are  <a href="/wiki/Budesonide" title="Budesonide">budesonide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fluticasone" title="Fluticasone">fluticasone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mometasone" title="Mometasone">mometasone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ciclesonide" title="Ciclesonide">ciclesonide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-6"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Long-acting_beta-adrenoceptor_agonist" title="Long-acting beta-adrenoceptor agonist">Long-acting beta-adrenoceptor agonists</a> (LABA) such as <a href="/wiki/Salmeterol" title="Salmeterol">salmeterol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Formoterol" title="Formoterol">formoterol</a> can improve asthma control, at least in adults, when given in combination with inhaled corticosteroids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ducharme2010_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ducharme2010-192">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duc2009_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duc2009-193">[193]</a></sup> In children this benefit is uncertain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ducharme2010_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ducharme2010-192">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid20393943_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20393943-194">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duc2009_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-Duc2009-193">[193]</a></sup> When used without steroids they increase the risk of severe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Side-effect" title="Side-effect">side-effects</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fanta2009_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fanta2009-195">[195]</a></sup> and with corticosteroids they may slightly increase the risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cates2012_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cates2012-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18646149_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18646149-197">[197]</a></sup> Evidence suggests that for children who have persistent asthma, a treatment regime that includes LABA added to inhaled corticosteroids may improve lung function but does not reduce the amount of serious exacerbations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chau2015_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chau2015-198">[198]</a></sup> Children who require LABA as part of their asthma treatment may need to go to the hospital more frequently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chau2015_198-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chau2015-198">[198]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antileukotriene_agents" title="Antileukotriene agents">Leukotriene receptor antagonists</a> (anti-leukotriene agents such as <a href="/wiki/Montelukast" title="Montelukast">montelukast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zafirlukast" title="Zafirlukast">zafirlukast</a>) may be used in addition to inhaled corticosteroids, typically also in conjunction with a LABA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antileukotriene_agents_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Antileukotriene_agents-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cha2017_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cha2017-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22592708_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22592708-201">[201]</a></sup>  For adults or adolescents who have persistent asthma that is not controlled very well, the addition of anti-leukotriene agents along with daily inhaled corticosteriods improves lung function and reduces the risk of moderate and severe asthma exacerbations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cha2017_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cha2017-200">[200]</a></sup> Anti-leukotriene agents may be effective alone for adolescents and adults, however there is no clear research suggesting which people with asthma would benefit from anti-leukotriene receptor alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>  In those under five years of age, anti-leukotriene agents were the preferred add-on therapy after inhaled corticosteroids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-7"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bts2009p43_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-bts2009p43-203">[203]</a></sup> A 2013 Cochrane systematic review concluded that anti-leukotriene agents appear to be of little benefit when added to inhaled steroids for treating children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> A similar class of drugs, <a href="/wiki/Arachidonate_5-lipoxygenase" title="Arachidonate 5-lipoxygenase">5-LOX</a> inhibitors, may be used as an alternative in the chronic treatment of mild to moderate asthma among older children and adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antileukotriene_agents_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Antileukotriene_agents-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USFDA_Zileuton_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-USFDA_Zileuton-205">[205]</a></sup> As of 2013 there is one medication in this family known as <a href="/wiki/Zileuton" title="Zileuton">zileuton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antileukotriene_agents_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Antileukotriene_agents-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mast_cell_stabilizer" title="Mast cell stabilizer">Mast cell stabilizers</a> (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cromolyn_sodium" title="Cromolyn sodium">cromolyn sodium</a>) are safe alternatives to corticosteroids but not preferred because they have to be administered frequently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p213_149-4"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p213-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antileukotriene_agents_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Antileukotriene_agents-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oral <a href="/wiki/Theophylline" title="Theophylline">Theophyllines</a> are sometimes used for controlling chronic asthma, but their used is minimized because of their side effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-8"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Omalizumab" title="Omalizumab">Omalizumab</a>, a monoclonal Antibody Against IgE, is a novel way to lessen exacerbations by lessening the levels of circulating IgE that play a significant role at allergic asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-9"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solèr_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Solèr-206">[206]</a></sup></li>
<li>Anticholinergic medications such as ipratropium bromide have not been shown to be beneficial for treating chronic asthma in children over 2 years old,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> but is not suggested for routine treatment of chronic asthma in adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></li>
<li>There is no strong evidence to recommend <a href="/wiki/Chloroquine" title="Chloroquine">chloroquine</a> medication as a replacement for taking corticosteroids by mouth (for those who are not able to tolerate inhaled steroids).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Methotrexate is not suggested as a replacement for taking corticosteriods by mouth ("steroid sparing") due to the adverse effects associated with taking methotrexate and the minimal relief provided for asthma symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></li>
<li>Macrolide antibiotics, particularly the azalide macrolide azithromycin, are a recently added GINA-recommended treatment option for both eosinophilic and non-eosinophilic severe, refractory asthma based on azithromycin's efficacy in reducing moderate and severe exacerbations combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Azithromycin's mechanism of action is not established, and could involve  pathogen- and/or host-directed anti-inflammatory activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Limited clinical observations suggest that some patients with new-onset asthma and with "difficult-to-treat" asthma (including those with the asthma-COPD overlap syndrome - ACOS) may respond dramatically to azithromycin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> However, these groups of asthma patients have not been studied in randomized treatment trials and patient selection needs to be carefully individualized.</li></ul>
<p>For children with asthma which is well-controlled on combination therapy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inhaled_corticosteroids" title="Inhaled corticosteroids">inhaled corticosteroids</a> (ICS) and long-acting beta<sub>2</sub>-agonists (LABA), the benefits and harms of stopping LABA and stepping down to ICS-only therapy are uncertain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> In adults who have stable asthma while they are taking a combination of LABA and inhaled corticosteroids (ICS), stopping LABA may increase the risk of asthma exacerbations that require treatment with corticosteroids by mouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ahm2015_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ahm2015-217">[217]</a></sup> Stopping LABA probably makes little or no important difference to asthma control or asthma-related quality of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ahm2015_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ahm2015-217">[217]</a></sup> Whether or not stopping LABA increases the risk of serious adverse events or exacerbations requiring an emergency department visit or hospitalisation is uncertain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ahm2015_217-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ahm2015-217">[217]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Delivery_methods">Delivery methods</span></h4>
<p>Medications are typically provided as <a href="/wiki/Metered-dose_inhaler" title="Metered-dose inhaler">metered-dose inhalers</a> (MDIs) in combination with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asthma_spacer" title="Asthma spacer">asthma spacer</a> or as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry_powder_inhaler" title="Dry powder inhaler">dry powder inhaler</a>. The spacer is a plastic cylinder that mixes the medication with air, making it easier to receive a full dose of the drug. A <a href="/wiki/Nebulizer" title="Nebulizer">nebulizer</a> may also be used. Nebulizers and spacers are equally effective in those with mild to moderate symptoms. However, insufficient evidence is available to determine whether a difference exists in those with severe disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p250_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p250-218">[218]</a></sup> For delivering short-acting beta-agonists in acute asthma in children, spacers may have advantages compared to nebulisers, but children with life-threatening asthma have not been studied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> There is no strong evidence for the use of intravenous LABA for adults or children who have acute asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> There is insufficient evidence to directly compare the effectiveness of a metered-dose inhaler attached to a homemade spacer compared to commercially available spacer for treating children with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverse_effects">Adverse effects</span></h4>
<p>Long-term use of inhaled corticosteroids at conventional doses carries a minor risk of adverse effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Safe09_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Safe09-222">[222]</a></sup> Risks include <a href="/wiki/Oral_candidiasis" title="Oral candidiasis">thrush</a>, the development of <a href="/wiki/Cataract" title="Cataract">cataracts</a>, and a slightly slowed rate of growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Safe09_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-Safe09-222">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Rinsing the mouth after the use of inhaled steroids can decrease the risk of thrush.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Higher doses of inhaled steroids may result in lower <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bone_mineral_density" title="Bone mineral density">bone mineral density</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others_2">Others</span></h3>
<p>Inflammation in the lungs can be estimated by the level of exhaled <a href="/wiki/Nitric_oxide" title="Nitric oxide">nitric oxide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-227">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-228">[228]</a></sup> The use of exhaled nitric oxide levels (FeNO) to guide asthma medication dosing may have small benefits for preventing asthma attacks but the potential benefits are not strong enough for this approach to be universally recommended as a method to guide asthma therapy in adults or children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_227-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-227">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-228">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>When asthma is unresponsive to usual medications, other options are available for both emergency management and prevention of flareups. Additional options include:
</p>
<ul><li>Humidified <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">Oxygen</a> to alleviate <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(medical)" title="Hypoxia (medical)">hypoxia</a> if <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_saturation" title="Oxygen saturation">saturations</a> fall below 92%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BertrandSánchez2020_144-10"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandSánchez2020-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li>Corticosteroid by mouth are recommended with five days of <a href="/wiki/Prednisone" title="Prednisone">prednisone</a> being the same 2 days of <a href="/wiki/Dexamethasone" title="Dexamethasone">dexamethasone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> One review recommended a seven-day course of steroids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_sulfate" title="Magnesium sulfate">Magnesium sulfate</a> intravenous treatment increases bronchodilation when used in addition to other treatment in moderate severe acute asthma attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p373_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p373-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> In adults intravenous treatment results in a reduction of hospital admissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Low levels of evidence suggest that inhaled (nebulised) magnesium sulfate may have a small benefit for treating acute asthma in adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-234">[234]</a></sup> Overall, high quality evidence do not indicate a large benefit for combining magnesium sulfate with standard inhaled treatments for adults with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-234">[234]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heliox" title="Heliox">Heliox</a>, a mixture of helium and oxygen, may also be considered in severe unresponsive cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p373_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p373-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>Intravenous salbutamol is not supported by available evidence and is thus used only in extreme cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rodrigo_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-rodrigo-235">[235]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methylxanthines" title="Methylxanthines">Methylxanthines</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Theophylline" title="Theophylline">theophylline</a>) were once widely used, but do not add significantly to the effects of inhaled beta-agonists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rodrigo_235-1"><a href="#cite_note-rodrigo-235">[235]</a></sup> Their use in acute exacerbations is controversial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA_2011_page37_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA_2011_page37-236">[236]</a></sup></li>
<li>The dissociative anesthetic <a href="/wiki/Ketamine" title="Ketamine">ketamine</a> is theoretically useful if <a href="/wiki/Intubation" title="Intubation">intubation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_ventilation" title="Mechanical ventilation">mechanical ventilation</a> is needed in people who are approaching respiratory arrest; however, there is no evidence from clinical trials to support this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p399_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p399-237">[237]</a></sup></li>
<li>For those with severe persistent asthma not controlled by inhaled corticosteroids and LABAs, <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_thermoplasty" title="Bronchial thermoplasty">bronchial thermoplasty</a> may be an option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bronch10_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bronch10-238">[238]</a></sup> It involves the delivery of controlled thermal energy to the airway wall during a series of <a href="/wiki/Bronchoscopy" title="Bronchoscopy">bronchoscopies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bronch10_238-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bronch10-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> While it may increase exacerbation frequency in the first few months it appears to decrease the subsequent rate. Effects beyond one year are unknown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GINA_2011_page70_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-GINA_2011_page70-240">[240]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Monoclonal_antibody" title="Monoclonal antibody">Monoclonal antibody</a> injections such as <a href="/wiki/Mepolizumab" title="Mepolizumab">mepolizumab</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mepolizumab_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mepolizumab-241">[241]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dupilumab" title="Dupilumab">dupilumab</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dupilumab_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dupilumab-242">[242]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Omalizumab" title="Omalizumab">omalizumab</a> may be useful in those with poorly controlled atopic asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEJM2017_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-NEJM2017-243">[243]</a></sup> However, as of 2019 these medications are expensive and their use is therefore reserved for those with severe symptoms to achieve cost-effectiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> Monoclonal antibodies targeting <a href="/wiki/Interleukin_5" title="Interleukin 5">interleukin-5</a> (IL-5) or its receptor (IL-5R), including <a href="/wiki/Mepolizumab" title="Mepolizumab">mepolizumab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reslizumab" title="Reslizumab">reslizumab</a> or <a href="/wiki/Benralizumab" title="Benralizumab">benralizumab</a>, in addition to standard care in severe asthma is effective in reducing the rate of asthma exacerbations. There is limited evidence for improved health-related quality of life and lung function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></li>
<li>Evidence suggests that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sublingual_immunotherapy" title="Sublingual immunotherapy">sublingual immunotherapy</a> in those with both <a href="/wiki/Allergic_rhinitis" title="Allergic rhinitis">allergic rhinitis</a> and asthma improve outcomes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid23532243_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid23532243-246">[246]</a></sup></li>
<li>It is unclear if <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-invasive_positive_pressure_ventilation" title="Non-invasive positive pressure ventilation">non-invasive positive pressure ventilation</a> in children is of use as it has not been sufficiently studied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_medicine">Alternative medicine</span></h3>
<p>Many people with asthma, like those with other chronic disorders, use <a href="/wiki/Alternative_medicine" title="Alternative medicine">alternative treatments</a>; surveys show that roughly 50% use some form of unconventional therapy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blanc_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-blanc-248">[248]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shenfield_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-shenfield-249">[249]</a></sup> There is little data to support the effectiveness of most of these therapies.
</p><p>Evidence is insufficient to support the usage of <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C">vitamin C</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_E" title="Vitamin E">vitamin E</a> for controlling asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> There is tentative support for use of vitamin C in exercise induced bronchospasm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fish_oil" title="Fish oil">Fish oil</a> dietary supplements (marine n-3 fatty acids)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> and reducing dietary sodium<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> do not appear to help improve asthma control. In people with mild to moderate asthma, treatment with <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_D" title="Vitamin D">vitamin D</a> supplementation may reduce the risk of asthma exacerbations, however, it is not clear if this is only helpful for people who have low vitamin D levels to begin with (low baseline vitamin D).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-255">[255]</a></sup> There is no strong evidence to suggest that vitamin D supplements improve day-to-day asthma symptoms or a person's lung function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_255-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-255">[255]</a></sup> There is no strong evidence to suggest that adults with asthma should avoid foods that contain <a href="/wiki/Monosodium_glutamate" title="Monosodium glutamate">monosodium glutamate</a> (MSG).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-256">[256]</a></sup> There have not been enough high-quality studies performed to determine if children with asthma should avoid eating food that contains MSG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_256-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-256">[256]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Acupuncture" title="Acupuncture">Acupuncture</a> is not recommended for the treatment as there is insufficient evidence to support its use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p240_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p240-257">[257]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mccartney_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-mccartney-258">[258]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_ioniser" title="Air ioniser">Air ionisers</a> show no evidence that they improve asthma symptoms or benefit lung function; this applied equally to positive and negative ion generators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22972060_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22972060-259">[259]</a></sup> Manual therapies, including <a href="/wiki/Osteopathy" title="Osteopathy">osteopathic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chiropractic" title="Chiropractic">chiropractic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physical_therapy" title="Physical therapy">physiotherapeutic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_therapy" title="Respiratory therapy">respiratory therapeutic</a> maneuvers, have insufficient evidence to support their use in treating asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hondras_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-hondras-260">[260]</a></sup>  The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buteyko_breathing_technique" title="Buteyko breathing technique">Buteyko breathing technique</a> for controlling hyperventilation may result in a reduction in medication use; however, the technique does not have any effect on lung function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGMA08_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-BGMA08-150">[150]</a></sup>  Thus an expert panel felt that evidence was insufficient to support its use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p240_257-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p240-257">[257]</a></sup> There is no clear evidence that breathing exercises are effective for treating children with asthma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prognosis">Prognosis</span></h2>
<p>The prognosis for asthma is generally good, especially for children with mild disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> Mortality has decreased over the last few decades due to better recognition and improvement in care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHLBI07p1_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHLBI07p1-263">[263]</a></sup> In 2010 the death rate was 170 per million for males and 90 per million for females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GAR2014_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-GAR2014-264">[264]</a></sup> Rates vary between countries by 100 fold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GAR2014_264-1"><a href="#cite_note-GAR2014-264">[264]</a></sup>
</p><p>Globally it causes moderate or severe disability in 19.4 million people as of 2004 (16 million of which are in low and middle income countries).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> Of asthma diagnosed during childhood, half of cases will no longer carry the diagnosis after a decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El2010_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-El2010-75">[75]</a></sup> Airway remodeling is observed, but it is unknown whether these represent harmful or beneficial changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maddox_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maddox-266">[266]</a></sup> Early treatment with corticosteroids seems to prevent or ameliorates a decline in lung function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beckett_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-beckett-267">[267]</a></sup> Asthma in children also has negative effects on quality of life of their parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup>
</p>
